</div></figure>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>Unknown, 2021</td><td>Dillon Attard</td><td>Sliema, Malta</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/ypS03" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Victim describes his disbelief as $700,000 stolen in front of him</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-141.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-925" width="874" height="841" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-141.png 681w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-141-300x289.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 874px) 100vw, 874px"></figure></div>


<p>A man described in court on Monday how his crypto wallet of $700,000 was reduced to zero within seconds of handing over his mobile phone to a man now charged with fraud.</p>



<p>The 27-year old victim, Dillon Attard, took the witness stand to testify against Luke Milton, a 25-year old company director who is pleading not guilty to misappropriation and fraud, cryptocurrency theft, money laundering as well as various breaches of the Virtual Financial Assets Act.</p>



<p>The two had met for lunch at a Sliema restaurant after Milton sought help to make a €5,000 blockchain investment on the phone.</p>



<p>“I couldn’t believe my eyes when I took the mobile back and saw that my wallet balance was zero,” said the witness, his tone agitated as he recalled the events of that lunchtime meeting with the accused.</p>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote">
<p><em></em></p>



<p><em>I couldn’t believe my eyes when I took the mobile back and saw that my wallet was zero</em></p>



<p><em></em></p>
</blockquote>



<p>“As reality seeped in, I just snatched the phone. He didn’t resist. My only thought was to secure my funds,” Attard said, explaining that he had placed both phones next to each other, helplessly watching the outgoing transaction and realizing “the fraud in [his] face.”</p>



<p>His first thought had been to redirect the funds from the accused’s mobile back to his own crypto wallet, but he soon realised that the transaction was being sent to another trust wallet.</p>



<p>“Couldn’t you stop the outgoing transaction?” asked the prosecution.</p>



<p>“You can never stop a blockchain transaction once sent,” explained the victim, adding that reversal of the transaction was not possible without access to the decentralised wallet to which it was sent.</p>



<p>Magistrate Donatella Frendo Dimech said the public needed to be aware of the risks at play so as not to be cast under a shadow like the accused in the proceedings, nor land in a situation as alleged by the victim.</p>



<p>During his lengthy and somewhat technical testimony, Attard gave a step-by-step account of events leading up to that lunch on June 16 when 424,670.97 Unizen crypto currency tokens were allegedly siphoned from his virtual wallet right under his nose.</p>



<p>Although Attard had warned Milton about the volatility of the market that day, Milton had insisted on going ahead with the transaction, engaging Attard’s help in converting the currency.</p>



<p>That was when Attard handed over his mobile across the table, for his lunch companion to scan the barcode on his crypto wallet.</p>



<p>But in those brief seconds, Milton must have pressed the “maximization” button, then “send,” and finally “confirm,” all in rapid succession, Attard said, appearing agitated.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>And all the while Milton had been acting “as though everything was normal,” he recalled.</p>



<p>As reality dawned on him, Attard said he messaged two friends of his who were members of the police corps, alerting them to the suspect fraud and summoning them to his assistance.</p>



<p>Until police arrived on site, the suspect fraudster had taken back possession of his phone and refused to allow Attard to browse freely through its contents.</p>



<p>When police did turn up, Milton allegedly admitted to sending the transaction “but then didn’t know what happened,” seeking to shift blame onto Attard.</p>



<p>Milton had claimed that Attard had done something wrong when both phones were in his possession, the flustered witness concluded.</p>



<p>Attard said he tried to remain calm until police arrived at the restaurant, trying to keep an eye on Milton to stop him from deleting anything on his phone.</p>



<p>The episode had apparently been caught on footage from the restaurant, the witness added, as the accused sat motionless and expressionless throughout the testimony.</p>



<p>The two had met days before the incident after the victim had stumbled across a blockchain project while exploring the options of a cryptocurrency loan.</p>



<p>A series of phone calls from a male caller and a meeting at a Burmarrad office between the victim, the accused and a third party identified as Milton’s business partner eventually led to that fateful encounter when the swindle allegedly took place.</p>



<p>The case continues.</p>



<p>Inspector Anthony Scerri together with AG lawyers Karl Muscat and Francesco Refalo prosecuted.</p>



<p>Lawyers Charles Mercieca and Matthew Xuereb were defence counsel.</p>



<p>Lawyers Franco Debono and Marion Camilleri appeared parte civile.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>January 5, 2021</td><td>37 y/o man</td><td>Chai Wan, Hong Kong</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/ps31W" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Robbers take US$387,000 in cash, 15BTC from man after in-person trade</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-large-font-size"><strong>Gang of six rob more than HK$3 million in bitcoin from trader, flee after kicking him out of the car</strong></p>



<p>A 37-year-old male trader trying to capitalize on the surge of Bitcoin was robbed of around HK$3 million in cash — the value of 15 bitcoins — and two mobile phones, minutes after being lured into in-person transaction of the cryptocurrency.</p>



<p>The incident comes as more traders who want to avoid the hassle of paying the service fee of online Bitcoin transactions choose to sell bitcoins in person.</p>



<p>A gang of six South Asian men in their 30s remain at large after fleeing on Tai Tam Road, Chai Wan in two cars.</p>



<p>The trader surnamed Lee was left empty-handed, after the suspects ran away with HK$3 million cash that they pretended to pay him and Lee’s 15 bitcoins worth HK$235,000 each were transferred to bitcoin wallet, according to police.</p>



<p>The Standard Channel</p>



<p><a href="https://archive.is/o/ps31W/https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCWhX9cSjah-OKSxjgjPvJ5g" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"></a></p>



<p>Lee told police that he was picked up by two South Asian men posing as buyers in a white car outside a hotel in North Point around 5pm on Monday.</p>



<p>He was then driven to Chai Wan, during which he transferred 15 bitcoins to the duo on his mobile phones, while the pair handed him HK$3 million in cash.</p>



<p>But as Lee was counting his proceeds, the car pulled over on a hillside near Shan Tsui Court on Tai Tam Road.</p>



<p>Shortly afterwards, a black car arrived and four South Asian men jumped into the white car, snatched the banknotes and two mobile phones before fleeing the scene in the black car.</p>



<p>Later, the two buyers shouted at Lee: “Money is gone, get off my car!” and kicked him out of the car before driving away.</p>



<p>The incident came to light at around 8pm when Lee walked for about five minutes and approached a police officer at the nearby Hing Man Estate on Tai Tam Road.</p>



<p>Lee was not injured as police combed Hing Man Estate late Monday evening but to no avail.</p>



<p>The six suspects remained at large as of last night.</p>



<p>The case has been classified as robbery and is being investigated by the Eastern District Crime Squad.</p>



<p>&nbsp; Lee, who has been a full-time Bitcoin trader for seven years, agreed to make the transaction with the two buyers via WeChat at 1pm Monday.</p>



<p>He had also traded his bitcoins with the two for HK$1 million online Sunday night.</p>



<p>In 2018, a 34-year-old local male buyer was robbed of HK$1.4 million in cash following an in-person Bitcoin transaction hoax in North Point.</p>



<p>Trading bitcoins in person has become popular recently, in which the buyer will clarify the acceptable currencies, banknotes and payment forms with traders beforehand, as banks are more aggressively acting against Bitcoin companies.</p>



<p>Other means to purchase bitcoins, including through a Bitcoin ATM, a “Bitcoin Wallet” that can be downloaded on phones and computers and exchanges, are also popular.</p>



<p>The price of Bitcoin has surged five times in less than a year and hit an all-time high last Christmas and early this month.</p>



<p>At midnight yesterday, the price per bitcoin broke through US$31,000 (HK$ 240,335), according to CryptoCompare, a website that discusses the value of various cryptocurrencies.</p>



<p>About 18.5 million out of a total of 21 million bitcoins have been mined and all the bitcoins will be snapped up by 2040.</p>



<p>Once all the bitcoins have been mined, buyers will still be incentivized to process transactions with fees.&nbsp;</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>January 18, 2021</td><td>Unidentified Woman</td><td>Kwun Tong, Hong Kong</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/3mR44" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Gang snatches HK$3.5 million from trader at knifepoint</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-144.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-932" width="851" height="1107" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-144.png 604w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-144-231x300.png 231w" sizes="(max-width: 851px) 100vw, 851px"></figure></div>


<p>Hong Kong police are hunting for a gang of thieves who lured a female cryptocurrency trader to an office for a deal and robbed her of HK$3.5 million (US$448,700) in cash at knifepoint on Monday afternoon.</p>



<p>The robbery – the second such hold-up in two weeks – took place at the Ricky Centre on Chong Yip Street in Kwun Tong around 2.30pm, after the woman met a man posing as a buyer.</p>



<p>She had recently sold the man digital money in three transactions, each involving HK$600,000 to HK$700,000, according to police.</p>



<p>“Investigations showed she was paid HK$3.5 million in cash after using her iPhone to complete an online transaction and sell him USDT tokens,” a police source said, referring to a type of cryptocurrency.</p>



<p>“Soon after she was handed the money, three men carrying either a knife or a rod rushed out from a room and snatched the money and the iPhone from her at knifepoint.”</p>



<p>He said the four fled after locking the victim in the office. The source said the gang could have carried out the earlier deals to win her trust and pave the way for the hold-up.</p>



<p>The robbery came to light when the woman used her second phone to contact her husband, who then made an 999 emergency call to police.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/0231e9cccfb070a1652d8ce23efcda0017da83c1.webp" alt="The victim’s husband called police. Photo: Warton Li"></figure></div>


<p>The victim’s husband called police. Photo: Warton Li</p>



<p>Officers found the woman safe and uninjured in the office. According to the force, the office was recently rented out on a short-term lease and only had several items of furniture.</p>



<p>The source said the uncle of the woman, who drove her to the building and was waiting downstairs, saw four men run out and drive off in a delivery van before police arrived.</p>



<p>Officers mounted a search, but no arrests were made.</p>



<p>Detectives from the Kwun Tong criminal investigation unit are handling the case.</p>



<p>On January 4, a gang of robbers stole bitcoin valued at more than HK$3 million from another trader – a 37-year-old man – after he met them to make a transaction in their car. They later kicked him out of the vehicle on a hillside on Tai Tam Road in Chai Wan.</p>



<p>They first paid the victim with cash but took it straight back after he transferred 15 bitcoin.</p>



<p>Another source said before the robbery the victim had also made deals with two of the robbers who posed as buyers.</p>



<p>In the first 10 months of 2020, police handled 242 reports of robbery across the city, up 103 per cent from 119 cases over the same period in 2019. Some 210 robbery cases were reported in the whole of 2019, and 147 cases in 2018.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-145.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-933" width="898" height="507" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-145.png 818w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-145-300x169.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-145-768x434.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 898px) 100vw, 898px"></figure></div>

<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>January 23, 2021</td><td>Physical Exchange Employees</td><td>Osztyn, Poland</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/wip/YOvMq" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Two employees shot at physical Bitcoin exchange FlyingAtom</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>He shot during the attack on the exchange office.&nbsp;100 thousand&nbsp;awards for the indication</strong></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-146.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-934" width="842" height="815" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-146.png 584w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-146-300x291.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 842px) 100vw, 842px"></figure></div>


<p>The press officer of the Olsztyn police, Andrzej Jurkun, informed that the policemen were still conducting operational activities aimed at arresting the perpetrator of the currency exchange robbery.- The policemen secured the traces, surveillance camera recordings, and questioned the witnesses of the incident.&nbsp;A tracking dog with a guide was included in the activities, Jurkun informed on Saturday.&nbsp;He added that policemen and a prosecutor were working on the spot.Until late at night&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong><a href="https://archive.is/o/YOvMq/https://www.tvp.info/51937085/%20https://www.tvp.info/tag?tag=policja" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">, the police</a></strong>&nbsp;blocked many roads in Olsztyn, checking every car.&nbsp;City buses were also checked.&nbsp;On Saturday morning, you can move around the city without any problems.</p>



<h2>He shot company representatives</h2>



<p>On Friday after&nbsp;At 7:00 p.m., a masked attacker came to the FlyingAtom exchange office in Olsztyn, which sells Bitcoins and gold.&nbsp;<strong>The owner of the exchange office, Dawid Muszyński, said that the attacker took ounces of gold worth 450 thousand.&nbsp;zloty.&nbsp;</strong>and shot two company representatives – a man and a woman.</p>



<p>– Paweł’s condition is serious, our information shows that he is put into a pharmacological coma – said Muszyński on Saturday.</p>



<p><strong>FlyingAtom offers 100,000.&nbsp;rewards to the person who contributes to arresting the perpetrator of the robbery.</strong></p>



<h2>Checking the area</h2>



<p>Jurkun reported that police officers searched the nearby area and verified the monitoring recordings, but so far it has not led to the arrest of the perpetrator of the robbery.</p>



<p>The FlyingAtom exchange office is located on the fourth floor of a skyscraper in the center of Olsztyn.&nbsp;The same building houses, among others,&nbsp;Voivodship Labor Office.</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>February 4, 2021</td><td>Married Couple</td><td>Stockholm, Sweden</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/5qCBI" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Armed robbers invade home and force owners to hand over 1M+ SEK in BTC</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Armed Bitcoin League Intruded on Couple – Got Over Millions</strong></p>



<p>The armed robbers forced their way into the couple’s home and, at gunpoint, forced them to take bitcoin worth a million, according to Aftonbladet’s information.Police became suspicious of two running men – and were able to arrest one.- You had a gun and a knife when you forced your way in, says Commissioner Per Åkermark.One of the police’s radio cars was routinely passing a residential area in the northern parts of&nbsp;</p>



<p><a href="https://archive.is/o/5qCBI/https://www.aftonbladet.se/tagg/3d8192c5-a65a-4559-8762-af100f036b78" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Stockholm County</a>&nbsp;on Thursday evening last week when they saw two people running away from the houses.- They get suspicious and run after these two.&nbsp;It turns out that together with a third person they broke into a home of two spouses, armed with a gun and a knife, says Per Åkermark, commissioner and operational coordinator at the police in southern Roslagen.</p>



<p>&nbsp;It is an aggravated robbery and, as is almost always the case in such crimes, money, jewellery, watches or other valuable equipment are sought after.&nbsp;They were inside the home for 20–30 minutes.Several sources tell Aftonbladet that the armed robbers, two men and a woman, after sneaking into the couple’s house, forced them to transfer the cryptocurrency bitcoin to the amount of one million.&nbsp;They are said to have acted threateningly with their weapons and then fled from the home, after which one of the plaintiffs chased after them until the police showed up.</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/716fc8aa7daa64b4f3a39475d33b9f1282172df2.jpg" alt="Mounting.  Two men and a woman sneaked into the couple&#39;s house and forced them to transfer bitcoin to the amount of one million, according to Aftonbladet&#39;s information."></p>



<p>PHOTO: AFTONBLADE/GETTYMounting.&nbsp;Two men and a woman sneaked into the couple’s house and forced them to transfer bitcoin to the amount of one million, according to Aftonbladet’s information.Per Åkermark does not want to go into what the robbers came over for loot, but confirms that the suspects sneaked into the plaintiffs’ house.- You knock on the door and trick the target owners into simply opening.&nbsp;I cannot comment on the change for preliminary investigation technical reasons.&nbsp;Now we are trying to find this motive image and clarify it, what did the perpetrators know before they committed this crime?Has&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>the loot been returned to the claimants?</strong></p>



<p>– We are working on that part now by going through IT equipment.</p>



<h2>More may be suspected</h2>



<p>Two of the three perpetrators are now in custody with restrictions, while the third, the woman, was released.&nbsp;The two arrested men are both in their 20s.</p>



<p><strong>Are all three still suspects?</strong>– The third was released, but we continue to investigate.&nbsp;There may be additional suspects, there may be individuals who planned or organized this in addition to those who carried it out.</p>



<p><strong>Intruding like this, how common is it?</strong>– It is not rare.&nbsp;One should not worry as a common man, but it has happened before and it happens at regular intervals.</p>



<p><strong>Do you have set targets, or does it happen a lot by chance?</strong>– A few years ago we had a similar incident in Djursholm, people resorted to keys and exclusive cars.&nbsp;There it may be that they understand that there are objects with high values.&nbsp;In some cases, criminals may seek out other criminals to settle debts, but it may also be the case that one is aware that the plaintiff posted an expensive item on a sales site or the like.</p>



<h2>“They do what it takes”</h2>



<p>Lotta Mauritzon is a crime prevention officer at the police’s national fraud center within Noa, National Operative Department.&nbsp;Crimes linked to bitcoin are becoming more common, she believes, and says that it is difficult to access someone else’s virtual currencies.- You must have login details to enter a virtual wallet where bitcoin and other currencies can be located.&nbsp;If someone else wants to access it, they will do what it takes, I think.She does not know the current case, but says that it sounds likely that the perpetrators knew in advance that the plaintiffs had bitcoin in their possession.</p>

<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>February ?, 2021</td><td>Swiss &amp; German</td><td>Gujranwala, Pakistan</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/Nmdes" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Armed robbers take $93k in BTC at gunpoint</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-147.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-937" width="880" height="1395" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-147.png 521w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-147-189x300.png 189w" sizes="(max-width: 880px) 100vw, 880px"></figure></div>


<p>GUJRANWALA: Two men have been arrested in Gujranwala for their involvement in what is being reported as Pakistan’s first Bitcoin robbery.</p>



<p>Two foreign nationals visiting Lahore on business had been taken hostage at gunpoint by the suspects. They stole cryptocurrency worth millions from them.</p>



<p>The police says the prime suspect is still at large.</p>



<p>Read more:&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/Nmdes/https://www.geo.tv/latest/335286-bitcoin-rises-above-50000-to-a-new-record-high" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><strong><em>Bitcoin rises above $50,000 to a new record high</em></strong></a></p>



<p>The victims were Swiss and German citizens. The suspects robbed Rs14.7 million worth of cryptocurrency from them.&nbsp;</p>



<p>A man named Rana Irfan is suspected of inviting the foreigners to Lahore by tricking them into making an investment.</p>



<p>An FIR has been registered at the Race Course police station. It says Irfan invited Stephen and Maria to Lahore and kidnapped them, along with three others, from a local five star hotel as he took them on a ride “to show them the city”.</p>



<p>Read more:&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/Nmdes/https://www.geo.tv/latest/324846-shc-restrains-authorities-from-taking-action-against-digital-currency-traders" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><strong><em>SHC restrains FIA from harassing Bitcoin, other cryptocurrency dealers in Pakistan</em></strong></a></p>



<p>The suspects reportedly sprinkled heroin on the foreigners and threatened to expose them as drug smugglers, after which they transferred Rs14.7 million of cryptocurrency to their account.</p>



<p>Police said the two accused were taken into custody from Gujranwala with the help of their vehicle numbers.&nbsp;</p>

<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March 10, 2021</td><td>Bank director</td><td>Recife, Brazil</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/KrFtE" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Man kidnapped by a gang , tied up, and had two teeth knocked out. He was released after he instructed his partner to transfer 4.78 BTC to the attackers.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-148-1024x786.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-939" width="1054" height="809" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-148-1024x786.png 1024w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-148-300x230.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-148-768x589.png 768w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-148.png 1048w" sizes="(max-width: 1054px) 100vw, 1054px"></figure></div>


<p>A Brazilian who owns a digital bank in Recife (PE) was kidnapped by a gang of criminals on March 10, 2021, losing 4.78 bitcoins after serious threats against his life.The case continues to be investigated by the Civil Police and the Public Ministry of Pernambuco, who have denounced ten people for their involvement with the crime.During the action, criminals asked for 100 bitcoins as a ransom for the victim, who was tied up without the amount to pay.&nbsp;Serious threats were made against his wife and daughter as well, and negotiations advanced.At one point, the criminals reduced the order to 50 bitcoins and continued with serious threats.&nbsp;After extensive negotiation, the ransom amount dropped to 6 bitcoins, when the director of the digital bank suffered an assault from the leader of the kidnapping.</p>



<h2>Brazilian owner of digital bank loses 4.8 bitcoins in kidnapping</h2>



<p>At the time, in March 2021,&nbsp;</p>



<p><a href="https://archive.ph/o/KrFtE/https://livecoins.com.br/bitcoin" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">bitcoin</a>&nbsp;was going through one of its biggest highs in history and its price reached values ​​in reais above R$ 300 thousand per unit.Thus, a criminal group approached a director of a digital bank in Recife, aware of all the details of his personal and professional life, then carrying out serious threats against his family members.After the negotiation between the parties indicated that 6 bitcoins should be the ransom value, the director told the kidnappers that he would call his partner, confessing that he was being kidnapped so that he would release the requested amount.At that moment, a fourth member of the group was called and, introducing himself as the head of the kidnapping, punched him in the mouth that broke two of his teeth.&nbsp;The victim, stunned and bleeding, called his partner, who began transferring amounts to the kidnappers’ wallet, totaling 4.78 bitcoins sent to the kidnappers.</p>



<h2>Victim undergoes therapy</h2>



<p>In the part of the process that&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>Livecoins</strong>&nbsp;had access to, the victim left the episode with serious psychological problems, going through therapy, doctors and other health professionals, already spending more than R$ 100 thousand to recover from the trauma.After the episode, the criminals were identified by the investigation and their assets were seized in civil police operations, such as luxury vehicles.&nbsp;Justice assessed that the moral damage suffered by the victim must be paid jointly by the 10 identified criminals, in the amount of R$ 250 thousand.In tracking the stolen bitcoins, no value was found, as the organization managed to pulverize the value on internet platforms abroad.In addition, all the goods that were seized must be auctioned so that the value remains in fiat currency, safeguarding the value for return to the victim.&nbsp;This Wednesday (26), the Justice of Pernambuco handed over the records of its recent decision to the prosecutor who is handling the case.</p>



<p><strong>To preserve the identity of the criminals and victims, as well as the target company, names will not be released.</strong>It is worth remembering that bitcoin investors in Brazil have been victims of gangs specializing in these robberies.&nbsp;Thus, it is important to avoid commenting on the subject in public, as well as showing investments in social networks.</p>



<p></p>

<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March 16, 2021</td><td>29 y/o Berlin man</td><td>Munich, Germany</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/H8Qix" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Robbers steal bitcoin worth almost 100,000 Euros</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Bitcoin robbery in Munich: perpetrators steal virtual money worth almost 100,000 euros</strong></p>



<h2>A 29-year-old from Berlin wanted to trade Bitcoins in a parking lot in Munich-Feldmoching on Tuesday.&nbsp;When he tried to show the supposed buyers the wallet with a high five-digit amount on his cell phone, the smartphone was snatched from him.&nbsp;The four perpetrators then fled in two cars.&nbsp;The police were able to locate and arrest the men from the Mühldorf district.</h2>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter" id="attachment_46701"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/f8473aacd5f4e34584b006da9e97dd722dfab62e.jpg" alt="Blue light police car"><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Blue light police car</figcaption></figure></div>


<p>As early as Tuesday, March 16, 2021, at around 7 p.m., a 29-year-old from Berlin met two unknown men in a parking lot on Dülferstrasse in Munich-Feldmoching.&nbsp;It was about a bitcoin business.&nbsp;The Berliner unlocked his smartphone and showed the men the contents of his electronic purse, the so-called wallet, which contained an amount in the high five-digit range.&nbsp;At that moment he was attacked by two other men.&nbsp;They grabbed and hugged him and snatched his mobile phone from his hand.&nbsp;The suspects then fled in two different vehicles.&nbsp;The 29-year-old from Berlin immediately notified the police and one of the two vehicles was found as part of the search.&nbsp;Inside were three suspects aged 21 to 29 from the Mühldorf district who were arrested.&nbsp;The second car could not be located.&nbsp;However, the police later arrested the fourth suspect, a 30-year-old from the Mühldorf district, after further investigation and search measures in Munich.&nbsp;Arrest warrants have been issued for three of the Bitcoin robbers.&nbsp;The investigations into this virtual money robbery are underway at Commissariat 21.</p>



<p></p>

<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March 18, 2021</td><td>“F.T.”</td><td>Mendoza, Argentina</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/DpOQe" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Armed robbers steal iPhone, $5k at gunpoint</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-149.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-944" width="882" height="882" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-149.png 750w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-149-300x300.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-149-150x150.png 150w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-149-500x500.png 500w" sizes="(max-width: 882px) 100vw, 882px"></figure></div>


<p>This Thursday, a&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>26-year-old man</strong>&nbsp;was the victim of crime and deception.&nbsp;The incident occurred around 7:30 p.m. on Calle 2 de Mayo and Severo del Castillo in the department of&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>Guaymallén.</strong></p>



<p><strong>The robbery occurred when the man was going to the place to sell the bitcoin&nbsp;</strong>&nbsp;virtual currency to some people&nbsp;and at one point some criminals surprised him and stole an&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>iPhone, 120 thousand pesos and 2,500 dollars.</strong>Hours later,&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>police personnel</strong>&nbsp;found the iPhone in the weeds of a vacant lot on Reconquista streetThe Fiscal Office No. 19 of the 35th Police Station intervened in the case.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>April 8, 2021</td><td>30 year old miner</td><td>Zaporizhya, Ukraine</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/WT3sm" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Mining farm owner shoots at looters</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/211315fa61aec8557eb3a58bbcd6eb27e812e8a5.jpg" alt="At the scene"></p>



<p>At the scene</p>



<p><strong>On April 8, at 8:40 p.m., the police station No. 4 of the Pologivskyi district administration of the National Security Service in the Zaporizhia region was informed that shots were heard in the yard of a house on Ivan Mazepa Street in Orihiv.&nbsp;Law enforcement officers arrived at the scene.</strong>It was established that three unknown persons, being in the yard of a local resident born in 1990, sprayed a gas canister and tried to take possession of the Bitcoin Antminer S9 mining equipment.&nbsp;Its cost is about 40 thousand hryvnias.However, the owner fought back and fired several shots from his Fort-12RM trauma pistol upwards and one shot at the feet of the attackers.&nbsp;After that, the attackers ran away.</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/553e6e84f2f54acd690307480e59be7d5d5813f7.jpg" alt="At the scene"></p>



<p>At the scenePolice officers immediately detained two men, and another escaped in a Zhiguli car.&nbsp;However, the “Interception” operation put into effect left him no chance to escape.The personnel of the regional police quickly focused on the search for the intruder, provided his signs and the license plates of the car.&nbsp;Soon the suspect was identified by the employees of the response group of the patrol police in the area of ​​the Orihiv bus station.As it turned out later, he changed the number plates on the car, left it in the forest, and tried to take the bus himself.</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/d858212c2909fb45bdbcbebaaed5cf14005da913.jpg" alt="At the scene"></p>



<p>At the sceneIt is now known that all participants in the offense are residents of the Dnipropetrovsk region, born in 1991, 1992 and 1993.&nbsp;They were detained in accordance with Article 208 of the Criminal Procedure Code of Ukraine.According to this fact, criminal proceedings have been opened under Clause 2 of Art.&nbsp;15 (Attempt to commit a crime), Part 2 of Art.&nbsp;186 (Robbery) of the Criminal Code of Ukraine.&nbsp;The issue of notifying the accused of suspicion and selecting a preventive measure in the form of detention is being resolved.</p>

<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>April 13, 2021</td><td>Undisclosed</td><td>Calgary, Alberta, Canada</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/GP76C" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Armed men force their way into Canyon Meadows home, steal cryptocurrency keys</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-150.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-945" width="873" height="1022" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-150.png 609w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-150-256x300.png 256w" sizes="(max-width: 873px) 100vw, 873px"></figure></div>


<p>Calgary police are asking the public to help identify a suspect linked to a violent home invasion earlier this week in the southwest community of Canyon Meadows.</p>



<p>Around midnight on April 13, two men armed with handguns forced their way into an apartment in the 11600 block of Elbow Drive S.W., police said.</p>



<p>The men tied up the apartment’s resident and stole computers, jewelry and bank cards from the suite. They also took cryptocurrency keys, which allow holders access to digital financial accounts.</p>



<p>The men forced the victim to disclose his bank PINs, then put him in a storage room and fled.</p>



<p>The victim, who sustained minor injuries, was able to free himself and call 911, police said.</p>



<p>A man later used one of the victim’s bank cards to withdraw money at an ATM in Crescent Heights, near the intersection of 12th Avenue and Centre Street N.E. The ATM recorded an image of the man, who is unknown to the victim.</p>



<p>Anyone with information on the crime or the suspects is urged to call the police non-emergency line at 403-266-1234. Anonymous tips can also be submitted to Crime Stoppers at&nbsp;1-800-222-8477 or&nbsp;calgarycrimestoppers</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>May, 2021</td><td>14 y/o boy</td><td>Bradford, UK</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/SUsgH" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Teen bitcoin trader kidnapped &amp; ransomed</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" width="927" height="801" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-151.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-946" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-151.png 927w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-151-300x259.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-151-768x664.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 927px) 100vw, 927px"></figure></div>


<p>A schoolboy who was thought to have made money trading in bitcoin was kidnapped by a gang who demanded £10,000 for his safe return, a court heard.</p>



<p>The 14-year-old, who cannot be named for legal reasons, was confronted outside a takeaway in&nbsp;<a href="https://www.theguardian.com/uk/bradford" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Bradford</a>&nbsp;in May and bundled into a car.</p>



<p>After one of the kidnappers put his hand over the boy’s mouth, the child was punched and forced into the back of a Toyota Auris.</p>



<p>Muhammed Khubaib, who owned the car, activated the vehicle’s central locking as the boy sat between two men in the back.</p>



<p>Khubaib, 22, then punched him in the face with a glove containing sand, Bradford crown court heard.</p>



<p>The prosecutor Laura McBride said the boy was told he would have to phone his mother and tell her to hand over “£10,000 or her son wouldn’t be going home”.</p>



<p>The boy’s mother was called and she described how the kidnappers demanded money while her son was crying, the court heard.</p>



<p>McBride said it was agreed the mother would give the men £900 and she came out of her home to hand over the cash when Khubaib drove the Auris to the house.</p>



<p>The incident was subsequently reported to the police and Khubaib was arrested a few days later.</p>



<p>He pleaded guilty to charges of kidnap and blackmail, but the court heard that the three other men involved had not been identified or prosecuted. Khubaib was sentenced to four years.</p>



<p>The recorder of Bradford, Judge Richard Mansell QC, said the boy had “clearly been targeted” by the men.</p>



<p>He said they kidnapped him after seeing social media posts that suggested he had made “a reasonable amount of money” from trading in bitcoin or other cryptocurrency.</p>



<p>The court heard the victim was no longer living in Bradford and Mansell said the offending had resulted in “profound consequences” for the youngster and his family.</p>



<p>Speaking after sentencing, DC Paul Maxwell of West&nbsp;<a href="https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>&nbsp;police said: “We welcome the sentence which has been passed down to Khubaib today at court. He pleaded guilty to both counts he was charged with in May.</p>



<p>“The victim, a young teenager, was vulnerable to criminal exploitation and Khubaib tried to exploit him for money.</p>



<p>“This was an incredibly distressing incident for both the victim and the victim’s mother, but thankfully both were not injured during the incident and have been given help and support by the police and partner agencies.”</p>



<h2></h2>



<p>… as you’re joining us today from Russia, we have a small favour to ask. Tens of millions have placed their trust in the Guardian’s fearless journalism since we started publishing 200 years ago, turning to us in moments of crisis, uncertainty, solidarity and hope. More than 1.5 million supporters, from 180 countries, now power us financially – keeping us open to all, and fiercely independent.</p>



<p>Unlike many others, the Guardian has no shareholders and no billionaire owner. Just the determination and passion to deliver high-impact global reporting, always free from commercial or political influence. Reporting like this is vital for democracy, for fairness and to demand better from the powerful.</p>



<p>And we provide all this for free, for everyone to read. We do this because we believe in information equality. Greater numbers of people can keep track of the events shaping our world, understand their impact on people and communities, and become inspired to take meaningful action. Millions can benefit from open access to quality, truthful news, regardless of their ability to pay for it.</p>



<p>Whether you give a little or a lot, your funding will power our reporting for the years to come.</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>May, 2021</td><td>___ Ghershony</td><td>Bethesda, Maryland</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/ezAnH" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Son drugs father, steals $400K in BTC</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-152.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-949" width="880" height="882" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-152.png 786w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-152-300x300.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-152-150x150.png 150w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-152-768x770.png 768w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-152-500x500.png 500w" sizes="(max-width: 880px) 100vw, 880px"></figure></div>


<p>The cup of warm tea seemed like a perfectly kind gesture. Even more so, court records show, when the server poured in some white powder for what he promised would beasafe energy boost.</p>



<p>“It’s really good for you,” Liam Ghershony, 24, told his father.</p>



<p>Unknown to the recipient, the powder was a benzodiazepine, a class of depressants that includes drugs like Xanax, and was delivered in a dose large enough to purposely knock him out. Then, free to use his father’s cellphone, Ghershony tapped through a two-step authorization to hack into a $400,000 cryptocurrency account.</p>



<p>“It didn’t have to be like this!” he wrote in notes he left behind for his father, adding that he was trying to help them both. “I’m gonna give you the best retirement.”</p>



<p>Two days later — after a worried friend of the older Ghershony couldn’t reach him and called the police — officers found him on his bedroom floor, breathing but unresponsive. He was rushed to a hospital, where he spent four days recovering from severe dehydration and acute organ dysfunction.</p>



<p>“It was outrageous,” Montgomery County Circuit Judge David Lease later told Liam Ghershony at the recent conclusion to his criminal case. “It was just beyond the pale.”</p>



<p>It was also — for all its bizarre particulars — a case that covered morecommon grounds: domestic violence; mental illness; the crippling effects of benzodiazepine abuse; and, for the parents of drug addicts, the steep challenges of when to extend another chance and when to set hard boundaries.</p>



<p>Ghershony, now 25, was initially charged by police with attempted murder — a count prosecutors soon learned overstated his intentions. He pleaded guilty to felony assault, spent 125 days in jail and was spared further punishment by undergoing two months of residential drug and mental health treatment. The sentence reflected his lack of a criminal record, his parents’ wishes and Lease’s calculation that rehab was the best course.</p>



<p><em>[<a href="https://archive.is/o/ezAnH/https://www.washingtonpost.com/health/2020/07/01/coronavirus-drug-overdose/?itid=lk_interstitial_manual_15" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Drug overdoses are soaring during the coronavirus pandemic</a>]</em></p>



<p>“I did a lot of crazy and messed up stuff when I was using,” the younger Ghershony said in an interview. “I will carry that with me — the guilt and the shame. And I want to take that on as I throw myself into recovery.”</p>



<p>The only child to parents who divorced when he was 3, Ghershony grew up in the&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/ezAnH/https://www.washingtonpost.com/realestate/budding-families-and-camaraderie-in-north-bethesdas-old-georgetown-village/2021/12/08/2fb76e98-5475-11ec-9267-17ae3bde2f26_story.html?itid=lk_inline_manual_18" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">affluentsuburb of Bethesda</a>&nbsp;just north of Washington. He excelled in competitive tennis and, after high school, he started an online clothing consignment business.</p>



<p>Ghershony began advising his father on a relatively new form of investing through cryptocurrencies, which are essentially online computer codes that allow people to store and send value online. The older Ghershony found it helpful.</p>



<p>“He’d said, ‘Dad, you’re too emotional. You’re too attached to the coin,’ ” the father recalled in an interview.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/fb6763de20708ca0de287dc38dd52a73030154c6.webp" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022"><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Among evidence in the case was a note written by Liam Ghershony to his father, which was left behind on the night Ghershony spiked his dad’s tea to access a locked cryptocurrency account. (Photo from Case evidence file)</figcaption></figure></div>


<p>The Washington Post generally does not identify victims of violent crimes without their consent. The older Ghershony, who spoke on the condition that his first name not be used, said he made his son a partner in a $100,000 investing account. As it soared in value, the two cashed out part of their crypto holdingsin 2018 and earned an after-tax profit of about $350,000, according to the father and son.</p>



<p>The younger Ghershony’s use of drugs, though, began to spiral. He took massive amounts of benzodiazepines coupled with Adderall and cocaine, according to court records. He blacked out daily, rotating from his condo to living with family to going missing.</p>



<p>“I thought I was going to lose him,” the older Ghershony said.</p>



<p>As his son’s paranoia grew, so too did his fixation with the plummeting price of their bitcoin holdings. But by then, the older Ghershony — concerned over his son’s judgment — had put the two-step lock on their investment accounts.</p>



<p>“Dad you need to sell,” the older Ghershony recalled his son telling him.</p>



<p>“No, you need to stop doing drugs,” the father responded.</p>



<p>Liam Ghershony soon launched his hacking plan. He had spent theday helping move furniture into his dad’s loft apartment in the Bethesda Row district. They ate dinner at a nearby restaurant and returned to the apartment where the younger Ghershony fixed two mugs of the powder-spiked, ostensibly energy-inducing tea, according to court records.</p>



<p>The concoction quickly put his dad to sleep, concerning enough to the younger Ghershony that he fastened an Apple Watch around his dad’s wrist to monitor his heartbeat. Then, using his dad’s phone for authorization, he moved $400,000 of bitcoin to an account he could control, and converted two-thirds of it to another cryptocurrency, Ethereum.</p>



<p>Ghershony left his dad passed out and alone in the apartment under the assumption he’d wake up, Ghershony said in an interview. But he failed to realize the effect of such adose of a benzodiazepine on a non-addict. “I obviously had a massive tolerance,” he said.</p>



<p>In the days after, though, Ghershony grew worried as hecouldn’t reach his dad on his phone or get him to answer his locked door. He called his father’s ex-girlfriend, who couldn’t reach him either, and she called 911 asking that officers go check on him. They found the older Ghershony on his floor but didn’t immediately know about the tea.</p>



<p>That began to change on May 14 when Liam Ghershony’s mother, Christine Prefontaine, called police to report that her son had admitted to“dosing”his father.</p>



<p><em>[<a href="https://archive.is/o/ezAnH/https://www.washingtonpost.com/health/2021/07/14/drug-overdoses-pandemic-2020/?itid=lk_interstitial_manual_40" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Drug overdose deaths soared to a record 93,000 last year</a>]</em></p>



<p>For Prefontaine, the call represented a mix of terror, opportunity and affection. Over the previous 18 months, she had persuaded her son to enter twodrug treatment programs, only to see him relapse. She’d also told him he couldn’t stay with her and her husband if he was actively using.</p>



<p>“I very strategically made a case against my son to force him into care and to protect our community,” Prefontaine said in an interview.</p>



<p>Detectives visited the older Ghershony in the hospital. He remembered his son served him tea that was supposed to give him more energy, according to records in the case, but said he told the detectives he had no memory of what happened next.</p>



<p>“I’m worried about my son, of course,” he told them, according to records in the case. “He’s a good kid overall.”</p>



<p>Five days later, detectives charged the younger Ghershony with attempted first-degree murder. As prosecutors later dug into the case, though, they found no evidence he purposely tried to kill his father.</p>



<p>“However, there was an intent to inflict serious bodily injury by the drugging, by the causing him to be unconscious,” Assistant State’s Attorney Donna Fenton said in court, adding, “But for the grace of God, Mr. Ghershony is still with us.”</p>



<p>She and Ghershony’s attorney, Steve Chaikin, worked out a plea agreement to a first-degree assault charge. A behavioral health expert who had evaluated Liam Ghershonytestified at his sentencing, attributingthe crime toanxiety and addiction to benzodiazepines.</p>



<p>Abuse of the drugs, nationwide, goes relatively unnoticed compared to opiates and cocaine, said Keith Humphreys, an addictions expert and psychiatry professor at Stanford University. Every year, he said, about 2,000 people fatally overdose from the drug and another 8,000 die after combining benzodiazepines with another substance.</p>



<p>People who use benzodiazepines legally often see their anxieties calmed through prescriptions. At increased doses though, the drug can produce wild mood swings, rendering the anxieties someone sought to calm more pronounced and more debilitating, Humphreys said. In that context, Humphreys said, knocking out your father to hack into a crypto account might seem rational.</p>



<p>“That’s the power of that drug,” Humphreys said, “and the power it has to change us.”</p>



<p><em>[<a href="https://archive.is/o/ezAnH/https://www.washingtonpost.com/outlook/2022/01/09/forgotten-approach-drug-addiction-recovery-may-yield-results-today/?itid=lk_interstitial_manual_55" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">A forgotten approach to drug addiction recovery may yield results today</a>]</em></p>



<p>Fenton, the prosecutor, cited past instances when the younger Ghershony had assaulted his father. She said those cases hadn’t been reported, as often happens among family members.</p>



<p>“This is a domestic violence case,” Fenton said in court. “This is a father and a son, not our typical couple that we would see.”</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/edfd6894e796684c51b5dd1115ce1cd76bbe1d1f.webp" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" width="383" height="197"><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Liam Ghershony embraced drug treatment and recovery after pleading guilty to first-degree assault in Montgomery County, Md. (Photo obtained by The Washington Post)</figcaption></figure></div>


<p>She asked for more local jail time followed by a lengthy period of “suspended” backup time that could send him to a prison within the Maryland Division of Correction (DOC) if he were to violate the terms of his probation.</p>



<p>Lease ordered drug treatment and imposed 20 years of suspended time, warning him: “If there’s an act of violence subsequent to this, you go to the DOC.”</p>



<p>Ghershony now lives in a group house in Rockville with other recovering addicts and takes part in outpatient drug treatment. He has been working on repairs to his Subaru with his dad. They meet regularly and talk about Liam’s intention to pursue a career in industrial design.</p>



<p>It’s left his father optimistic, noting his son is more interested in addiction-recovery meetings than past forms of socialization: “If someone wants to meet him and they’re from the past, he tells them they have to meet him at a meeting.”</p>



<p>Ghershony’s attorney, Chaikin, has interacted with the parents of drug addicts throughout his career — as a prosecutor, a defense attorney and as a regular speaker to parent groups and schools.</p>



<p>“Calling the police on your child is excruciating. It’s often a last resort,” he says, repeating a theme in his talks, “but it’s a lot less painful than burying your child.”</p>



<p>Ghershony’s mother, Prefontaine, a professional in the field of public health and Human Centered Design said too often parents like her become “polarized between ‘being powerless’ and ‘involving the criminal system.’”</p>



<p>But she sees a change in her son. “I hear him being serious about treatment in a way that he’s never been,” she said. “He’s back to being the kinder version of himself.”</p>



<p>Ghershony recently started a job waiting tables at a restaurant in Rockville.</p>



<p>“I definitely have said I’m sorry to my dad,” he said. “But I feel like I can say only so much. I need to show him, and myself, through actions how much I’ve changed.”</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-text-color has-alpha-channel-opacity has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812;color:#f78da812">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>June 11, 2021</td><td>40 y/o man</td><td>Gyeonggi Province, South Korea</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/e6FKx" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Woman drugs man she met on chat app, steals $87K from his phone.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-153.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-952" width="897" height="863" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-153.png 771w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-153-300x289.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-153-768x740.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 897px) 100vw, 897px"></figure></div>


<p>A South Korean woman who met a man on a smartphone chat app, drugged him, and stole USD 87,000 in crypto from his phone has been sentenced to five years in prison.</p>



<p><a target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener" href="https://newsis.com/view/?id=NISX20220520_0001879422">Per</a>&nbsp;Newsis, the Suwon District Court heard how a 20-year-old woman (named by the court as A) met a man via an app and then arranged to meet him on June 10, 2021. In the early hours of June 11, the duo went to a “love motel” in Gyeonggi Province. The man, who is in his 40s and was named by the court as B, had told A about the scale of his crypto holdings during their conversation on the chat app platform.</p>



<p>But the court heard that A then proceeded to lace B’s drink with sleeping pills, before using his phone to transfer tokens from a smartphone-based crypto wallet to her own wallet.</p>



<p>EDaily&nbsp;<a target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener" href="https://www.edaily.co.kr/news/read?newsId=02102486632331544">reported</a>&nbsp;that the smartphone in question was protected with a fingerprint sensor – but that A was able to press B’s finger against the sensor to unlock the device while he was unconscious.</p>



<p>When B regained consciousness, he confronted A, who then proceeded to threaten him with telling B’s family about the “sordid” nature of their encounter.</p>



<p>B proceeded to report the incident to the police – but A attempted to confuse the police officers who questioned her by claiming that B had in fact raped her, and had given her the crypto in an attempt to silence her.</p>



<p>The court and presiding judge Hwang In-seong found A guilty of robbery, threatening behavior, and injury, as well as violations of the Drug Management Act. She was also found guilty of perverting the course of justice.</p>



<p>The judge stated that the sentence was justified due to the fact that the amount of crypto holdings stolen was high, and that A had attempted to sow the seeds of confusion in the ensuing police investigation.</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>June 14, 2021</td><td>22 y/o man</td><td>Kwun Tong, Hong Kong</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/6h6UG" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Trader temporarily blinded, HK$2 million stolen</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-154.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-957" width="881" height="1249" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-154.png 562w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-154-212x300.png 212w" sizes="(max-width: 881px) 100vw, 881px"></figure></div>


<p>A citywide police hunt is under way for a gang of thieves after a cryptocurrency trader was sprayed in his eyes with an unknown substance and robbed of HK$2 million while he was on his way to buy bitcoin in Hong Kong on Tuesday.</p>



<p>The suspects struck in broad daylight in the car park of Legend Tower on Shing Yip Street in Kwun Tong, shortly before 4.30pm.</p>



<p>According to police, the 22-year-old victim was targeted after he parked his car.</p>



<p>“While he was waiting for a lift, two men approached him and sprayed an unknown liquid into his eyes before snatching his green bag containing HK$2 million,” a police spokesman said, adding the victim said the substance had left him briefly unable to see.</p>



<p>Officers said the two robbers fled in a white car driven by a third man, the three suspects later abandoned the car at the junction of Hoi Yuen Road and Shing Yip Street, and fled on foot heading towards Wai Yip Street.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/936227c9ec17d08fc9a3673121cffc3b23f5d46f.webp" alt="Crimes surrounding the purchase of bitcoin have jumped in Hong Kong since the start of the year. Photo: Reuters"></figure>



<p>Crimes surrounding the purchase of bitcoin have jumped in Hong Kong since the start of the year. Photo: Reuters</p>



<p>Officers combed the area, but no arrests were made. The spokesman said the victim did not request hospital treatment in the incident.</p>



<p>In March, two money exchange company employees were lured to a Tin Hau shop and conned out of HK$3.85 million in a bogus bitcoin transaction.</p>



<p>In January, two cryptocurrency traders were robbed of HK$6.5 million in total in two separate cases in a fortnight.</p>



<p>On January 4, a gang of robbers lured a 37-year-old man to transfer bitcoin valued more than HK$3 million to them after he met them and made an online transaction in their car. They first paid the victim with cash but took it straight back after he transferred bitcoin to them. The victim was later kicked out of the vehicle on a hillside on Tai Tam Road in Chai Wan.</p>



<p>Two weeks later, another gang lured a female trader to an office in Kwun Tong for a transaction and robbed her of HK$3.5 million at knifepoint.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>June 24, 2021</td><td>39 y/o man</td><td>Leeuwarden, Netherlands</td><td><a href="https://archive.md/xviCX" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">3 men posing as service technicians beat password out of Bitcoin owner</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Overvallers aan de haal met waardevolle cryptomunten</strong> </p>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Robbers make off with valuable crypto coins</strong></p>



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed aligncenter is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-block-embed-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<iframe loading="lazy" title="Leeuwarden: Overvallers aan de haal met waardevolle cryptomunten" width="640" height="360" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/tbPNNEP20pg.html" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe>
</div></figure>



<p></p>



<p>The 39-year-old resident of an apartment on Coopmansstraat in Leeuwarden was severely assaulted on June 24, 2021 during a robbery.&nbsp;The three perpetrators have been inside for more than an hour and stole valuable crypto coins.</p>



<p>At about 8.40 p.m. that Thursday, the victim was knocked on the door.&nbsp;Three men in green jackets pretended to be service technicians and asked if he had a malfunction.&nbsp;Before he knew it, he was grabbed by the throat and violently dragged into the living room, where he was beaten.&nbsp;The resident had to give the code to access his crypto coins under threat.</p>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote">
<p>They literally knocked the code out of me.”home robbery victim</p>
</blockquote>



<h3>Background</h3>



<p>The robbers were aware that the resident was in possession of crypto coins.&nbsp;He has discussed it with a number of people in his environment and that information may have ended up with the perpetrators via-via.&nbsp;Police are still investigating this scenario.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-embed aligncenter is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-block-embed-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio"><div class="wp-block-embed__wrapper">
<iframe loading="lazy" title="Leeuwarden, 24 juni 2021" width="640" height="360" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/yrX3iCG_Lsc.html" frameborder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen=""></iframe>
</div></figure>



<p>One of the perpetrators has a light-skinned complexion and is around 35 years old.&nbsp;Like the other two men, he wore a green jacket that night.</p>



<h3>Volkswagen Polo</h3>



<p>A few minutes before the robbery, a Volkswagen Polo was driving on Pasteurweg in Leeuwarden.&nbsp;Due to the time and direction of travel, the police think it may have been the perpetrators who drove this car.<br>If the Polo has nothing to do with the robbery, the police would like to speak with the occupant(s), but as an important witness(s).</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/csm_212565_ljouwert_bbpolo_828b1eaa62.jpg" alt="VW Polo on the Pasteurweg"><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">VW Polo on the Pasteurweg</figcaption></figure></div>


<h3>Cryptocurrencies ‘frozen’</h3>



<p>Cryptocurrency transactions are public.&nbsp;So the police can see exactly where the coins have been in recent months and where they are at the moment.<br>Specifically, the detective team was able to ‘freeze’ part of the loot, so that the criminals can’t do anything with it at the moment.&nbsp;The next step is to actually get those coins back from the victim.</p>

<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>July 14, 2021</td><td>Morakinyo Peter &amp; Yusuf Dayo</td><td>Lagos, Nigeria</td><td><a href="https://archive.md/Xdsmc" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Law Enforcement Officers rob 2 men of $50K USD in bitcoin at gunpoint</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-155.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-965" width="898" height="489" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-155.png 850w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-155-300x163.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-155-768x418.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 898px) 100vw, 898px"></figure></div>


<p>The Inspector-General of Police, Usman Alkali Baba, has ordered an immediate investigation into the professional misconduct, abuse of office and extortion of N22million worth of bitcoin from two young Nigerians, Morakinyo Tobiloba Peter and Yusuf Samson Dayo, by police officers in Lagos State.<br>SaharaReporters had reported that a Deputy Superintendent of Police with force number 14534, Cordelia Nwawe, one Inspector Austin and others, all attached to the Force Criminal Investigation Department Annex, Alagbon Close, Lagos extorted N22million worth of bitcoin from the two young men at gunpoint.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/ae5e96daef467b471209df6e8a960ed1cde91610.jpg" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022"></figure></div>


<p>Reacting in a statement on Monday, Force’s spokesman, Frank Mba said a Special Investigation Panel led by DCP Olaolu Adegbite would carry out a discreet and transparent investigation into the allegation has been inaugurated.<br>Mba added that DSP Cordelia and other police personnel indicted in the report had been ordered to report at the Force Headquarters, Abuja on Tuesday.<br>The statement read, “The Nigeria Police Force has commenced investigations into the alleged professional misconduct, abuse of office and extortion of Twenty-Two Million Naira worth of Bitcoin from some citizens in Lagos State, levelled against a Deputy Superintendent of Police, Nwawe Cordelia and others, serving at the Force Criminal Investigations Department (FCID), Alagbon, Lagos. This follows the setting up of a Special Investigation Panel by the Inspector General of Police, IGP Usman Alkali Baba, to carry out a discreet and transparent investigation into the allegation.<br>“This development has become imperative following the report making the rounds in the media alleging the involvement of the officers in the extortion of Twenty-Two Million Naira worth of Bitcoin from two young Nigerians, Morakinyo Tobiloba Peter and Yusuf Samson Dayo at gunpoint on July 14, 2021 while driving along the Ikoyi/Ajah Expressway, Lagos State.<br>“Consequently, DSP Cordelia and the other Police personnel allegedly indicted in the report, have been ordered to report to the Special Investigation Panel, Force Headquarters, Abuja, on Tuesday, 21st December, 2021 to answer to the allegations against them.<br>“The Special Investigation Panel is headed by DCP Olaolu Adegbite, MFR, of the Force Intelligence Bureau (FIB). The Force advices any member of the public who has had similar experiences of high-handedness or extortion by the officers in question, her team or any other officer at the FCID Alagbon to come forward with detailed information to enable the panel achieve a wholistic investigation.<br>“Meanwhile, it is vital to state that the alleged actions of the police officers in question do not represent the standards and practices of the Nigeria Police Force and as such any officer found wanting will be visited with the full wrath of the law. Members of the public are enjoined to remain calm as the Force will provide timely updates and make the outcome of the investigation public.”<br>SaharaReporters had on Sunday reported that the duo, both realtors told SaharaReporters that they were stopped on July 14, 2021 while driving along the Ikoyi/Ajah Expressway by a team of police officers in mufti led by Austin, who adopted a fictitious name “Osas.”<br>“We were driving on the Ikoyi/Ajah Expressway precisely at 1004 on the 14th of July 2021, when a team of police officers in mufti accosted us and ordered us to park. We parked and the police officers jumped into the car and ordered us to open our phones,” one of the victims had told SaharaReporters.<br>“Since we had nothing to hide, we gave them our phones and they found nothing incriminating. To our surprise, they ordered us to drive down to their office; we insisted we must know our offences before we can move down to the station. But the police officers descended on us and beat us for disobedience. They claimed we were too fresh not to be a fraudster. We begged them and showed them that we are realtors. We gave them our identity cards and showed them some of our ongoing projects but they insisted we were fraudsters.<br>“When we got to the police station at FCID Annex, Alagbon Close, Lagos, we were quickly pushed into the cell and they went away with our mobile phones. The police officers returned some hours later and told us we were trading in Bitcoins.<br>“Before we know it, they started beating us and calling us Yahoo boys, we told them we were not Yahoo boys. We explained that we are realtors and it was because of the decline in naira that we converted our money into bitcoin, but they kept beating us and they said we should write statement around 8:00pm in the night.”<br>The duo added that the statements written by them were torn into pieces by the policemen while they were forced to sign another one written by the officers alleging that they were internet fraudsters.<br>“We wrote the statements and they tore it into pieces and wrote another statement for us and forced us to sign it. We did signed the statement and they took them before their boss, DSP Cordelia Nwawe with force number 145341, Admin section, FCID Annex, Alagbon Lagos,” they added.<br>“Mrs Uwawe asked her officers what happened and they narrated the whole story to her, they told her we are Yahoo boys which we denied and the woman said they should give us bail condition, they demanded N20million from us and when we said we don’t have such amount of money, the woman said they should go and kill us if we insist we cannot pay them N20million as bail.<br>“Officer Austin who led the team also adopted a fictitious name so that people will not know his true name. He was addressed as Osas by DSP Uwawe, he was the one who took us to the cell and threatened to kill the two of us if we did not transfer the N20million in bitcoin to them.<br>“So when he bought out his gun and was taking us out of the cell to kill us as ordered by her boss, DSP Uwanue, we now succumbed to him and said he should remove the money from our account, he insisted he wanted bitcoin and not naira, he provided another bitcoin account and he transferred N22million equivalent of bitcoin from our account.”</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>July 28, 2021</td><td>39 y/o man</td><td>Tsim Sha Tsui, Hong Kong</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/CeCA8" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Trader robbed of HK$3 million at knifepoint</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>
