<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>February 3, 2022</td><td>Vinay Jain</td><td>Surat, India</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/hMOJh" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Auto parts businessman brings suitcase full of $260K worth of cash to do an in-person crypto trade, gets beaten and robbed by 8 men.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" width="1024" height="611" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-174-1024x611.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1007" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-174-1024x611.png 1024w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-174-300x179.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-174-768x459.png 768w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-174.png 1194w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px"></figure></div>


<p>SURAT: The hoax call about an alleged armed robbery at angadia firm opposite Varachha police station that led the police into a wild goose chase on Friday afternoon finally turned out to be a huge case of dacoity worth Rs 2 crore late on Saturday night.<br>While it had all happened right under the police’s nose, the entire episode got too confusing sans any complaints filed leading cops about to close the case as a hoax call. However, a Hyderabad-based victim emerged at the police station to file a complaint of dacoity.<br>The emergence of the victim, an auto parts businessman, cleared the picture after the pieces fit like a jig-saw puzzle, even as cops could not find a complainant then at the spot that day. Based on his complaint, Varachha police registered an offence of dacoity (IPC 395) against Pintoo Kumar&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/hMOJh/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/Jha" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Jha</a>, Amit,&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/hMOJh/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/Suman-Singh" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Suman Singh</a>, Madhukar, Rakesh, Raju, Vicky, Shahrukh and some other people.<br>According to the case details, Vinay Jain (29), a resident of Film Nagar in Hyderabad told the Varachha police that he had come to the city to invest in cryptocurrency after being lured by the accused, but instead got looted of Rs 2 crore.<br>“Around two months ago, Jain came in contact with one Lakshminarayan in Hyderabad who deals in cryptocurrency. Lakshminarayan lured Jain to invest in crypto for better returns, and after he agreed, introduced him to P K Jha.<br>After a few meetings with Jha in Hyderabad, Jain along with his brother Aakash, Lakhminarayan and driver&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/hMOJh/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/Shinu" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Shinu</a>&nbsp;drove down to Surat in his father’s Fortuner car on February 3. Before embarking on their Surat journey, Jain deposited Rs 6 crore in an angadia firm there which he later collected in Surat. Jain claimed he had collected the amount from his relatives to invest in crypto,” said the police.<br>The next day, Vinay Jain along with the three others reached the angadia firm named ‘Shree&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.is/o/hMOJh/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/Siddhi-Vinayak-Enterprise" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Siddhi Vinayak Enterprise</a>’ located at Central Bazar in Varachha with Rs 2 crore to open his crypto account. Jha took the cash amount from Jain, but the money did not get transferred in Jain’s account for a long time.<br>In the meantime, Jha prepared to leave the place with the cash, when Jain asked him to wait till the account showed his money.<br>This started an altercation when around eight other people joined him and started to thrash Jain and others before disappearing with the amount before cops reached the scene.<br>“It was a pre plan by the accused to beat them up and steal the cash. Jain and the other three left the city after the incident and reached Mumbai. However, they decided to file a police complaint and returned again to Surat on Saturday and filed a complaint,” cops added.</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>February 3, 2022</td><td>Ilya Basin</td><td>Brooklyn, New York</td><td><a href="https://archive.is/DEA2C" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Crypto consultant hog-tied, beaten during home invasion.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-175.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1010" width="891" height="1245" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-175.png 591w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-175-214x300.png 214w" sizes="(max-width: 891px) 100vw, 891px"></figure></div>

<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-176.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1011" width="915" height="1121" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-176.png 605w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-176-245x300.png 245w" sizes="(max-width: 915px) 100vw, 915px"></figure></div>


<p>.&nbsp;</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><a href="https://archive.is/o/DEA2C/https://nypost.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/2/2022/02/home-invasion-1.jpg?quality=90&amp;strip=all" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/820eba9a2835ad92dc456b71cf4cab4dbcbf28c2.webp" alt="The robbers ransacked Basin&#39;s bedroom and took a pair of designer watches worth more than $300,000."></a><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">The robbers ransacked Basin’s bedroom and took a pair of designer watches worth more than $300,000.</figcaption></figure></div>


<p>“As I opened it, they both bum-rushed me,” Basin said. “Maybe if I had some karate training, I would have acted differently, but my first instinct was to try to swing the door close[d].”</p>



<p>The ski-mask-wearing suspect then “took me down,” Basin said.</p>



<p>“I hit my head on the dog’s food bowl,” he added. “Once I was on the ground, they zip-tied my hands behind me. They put tape over my mouth and taped my ankles together.</p>



<p>“For the first minute or two, I was just hoping that I was going to wake up,” he recalled. “I didn’t think it was real. It happened so quick that I didn’t know what was going on. It [makes] no sense.”</p>



<p>One of the suspects is shown on the video wandering around the apartment and repeatedly asking, “Where’s the money?”</p>



<p>At one point, the same intruder kicked him in the face and told him to “shut up” as he whimpered on the ground.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image"><a href="https://archive.is/o/DEA2C/https://nypost.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/2/2022/02/home-invasion-2.jpg?quality=90&amp;strip=all" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/b7d3ee9cccde9ce7a1a4741ebb7c3d7c6eb9201c.webp" alt="Watches stolen in home invasion."></a><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">The home invaders took a Rolex Presidential watch from Basin.</figcaption></figure>



<p>In a separate video released by cops, the invader is shown rifling through the refrigerator. Basin said he took out French fries and blueberries, apparently to keep Smokey quiet.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The robber ultimately found the watches in their original boxes in Basin’s bedroom closet and stuffed them in a backpack.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The duo disconnected Basin’s Internet router and untied him before they bolted, according to the victim.</p>



<figure class="wp-block-image"><a href="https://archive.is/o/DEA2C/https://nypost.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/2/2022/02/home-invasion-8.jpg?quality=90&amp;strip=all" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/f45c54babda37342950221a76f136c04ff9f3391.webp" alt="home invasion "></a><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Basin said the terrifying ordeal went on for about 30 minutes.</figcaption></figure>



<p>Basin said the incident was “the most traumatizing thing that’s ever happened to me.”</p>



<p>“I’ve been living in this city since I was six years old,” Basin said. “This is my home, but this makes me feel like I should definitely get out of here. I don’t have enemies. I’m a sweetheart of a dude. It’s very shocking that this happened.”</p>



<p>He added that all his wealth was in those two watches.&nbsp;</p>



<p>“That’s all my money,” he said. “It’s literally all I have. It was my one hope of getting a house, getting out of here. It was my ‘one ticket’ situation to get a better life.”&nbsp;</p>



<p>Cops continued to search for the suspects Wednesday.</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March, 2022</td><td>bitcoin trader</td><td>Dubai, UAE</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/Ri5N9" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">4 men invade home, tie up man, steal $450K from safe.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-177.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1012" width="873" height="905" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-177.png 628w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-177-289x300.png 289w" sizes="(max-width: 873px) 100vw, 873px"></figure></div>


<p>Four Asian men have been jointly fined Dh1.7 million for assaulting a bitcoin trader and stealing the same amount from his residence.</p>



<p>Last March, a man reported that he had been attacked in his house and that Dh1.7 million had been stolen from a safe that belonged to his trading partner.</p>



<p>The man claimed in his testimony that a group of men reached his residence, and told him that his ‘address was incorrect’. When he attempted to close the door, the men pushed him and entered the house. After the man fell to the floor, the men put a knife to his neck.</p>



<p>The accused then tied him up with plastic rope and retrieved a key to the safe that was placed under a table. They then proceeded to steal the amount.</p>



<p></p>



<p>After the man managed to untangle himself, he called his partner and the police to inform them of the incident.</p>



<p>The second victim said in his testimony that he received a call from the first victim who informed him of the crime.</p>



<p>After he arrived at the spot, he saw the house in a mess and the safe open, with the cash missing.</p>



<p>Police investigations revealed that the criminals illegally infiltrated the country and fled after committing the crime.</p>



<p>Authorities then undertook a coordinated operation and managed to nab the culprits after zoning down on their location.</p>



<p>During interrogation, the men confessed to the crimes.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March 2, 2022</td><td>Unidentified man</td><td>Miami, FL</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/tyzQa" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Businessman ambushed by armed robber, has $1M watch &amp; crypto wallet taken.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" width="889" height="821" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-178.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1013" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-178.png 889w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-178-300x277.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-178-768x709.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 889px) 100vw, 889px"></figure></div>


<p>MIAMI (WSVN) – A South Florida businessman said he was ambushed by an armed robber who knew exactly what he wanted: his crypto wallet and his pricey watch.</p>



<p>The victim, who asked not to be identified or show his face on camera, said he was targeted as he arrived to his home in Miami’s Edgewater neighborhood, at around 11 p.m., Wednesday.</p>



<p>“I could have been dead,” he said.</p>



<p>Surveillance video recorded the terrifying moments.</p>



<p>The victim said he was coming from after a meeting when the unthinkable occurred.</p>



<p>“Pulls a gun, run towards me, put it onto my face and tells me, ‘Get on the ground! Give me everything you got!’” said the businessman.</p>



<p>Everything he had, the victim said, had a major price tag, beginning with a watch.</p>



<p>“That specific day, I took it out from the safe for that specific meeting, estimated at $400,000. It’s a Patek Philippe rose gold watch,” said the businessman. “When I purchased it, it wasn’t $400,000, way less. It was an investment, just like in the stock market.”</p>



<p>But thats not the only investment taken, according to the victim.</p>



<p>The businessman said the robber swiped his phone. On it was a crypto wallet, an app that serves as a bank for digital money.</p>



<p>The total of everything taken was a pretty penny.</p>



<p>“Estimated about a million dollars,” said the businessman.</p>



<p>He said he’s sharing his story with 7News in hopes that the bad guys are caught.</p>



<p>“I think I was targeted. Someone knew me, someone knew where I live. I don’t think it was a coincidence,” he said. “They knew where I lived. The car was already parked there.”</p>



<p>The surveillance video appears to show the robbers were waiting. They are seen pulling up and parallel parking moments before the victim arrived</p>



<p>The businessman said he fears someone else could strike.</p>



<p>“Another guy in the car, did a quick U-turn, jumped back to the car, then they flew off,” he said.</p>



<p>Now, the victim said, he’s moving out of Edgewater and is done investing in watches.</p>



<p>“This morning I made some phone calls. I’ve actually sold my watch collection,” he said. “I don’t want to wear anything expensive anymore. I don’t want anything on me that’s flashy.”</p>



<p>Police continue to investigate.</p>



<p>If you have any information on this robbery or the subjects’ whereabouts, call Miami-Dade Crime Stoppers at 305-471-TIPS. Remember, you can always remain anonymous, and you may be eligible for a reward of up to $5,000.</p>

<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March 4, 2022</td><td>Electronics Dealer</td><td>Pune, India</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/wPxv4" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Woman cop suspended for bid to extort crypto from trader</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Woman cop suspended for bid to extort crypto from trader</strong></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/550e7e22a1e8d682f42739f48aee7e6258b7090b.webp" alt="banner img"></figure></div>


<p>Pune: A woman constable from the Pune cyber police has been suspended following a suo motu inquiry by the city police over an information that she threatened and tried to extort an unspecified amount in the form of cryptocurrencies from a Wakad-based electronic goods dealer, who also deals in digital currencies.<br>Additional commissioner of police (crime) Ramnath Pokale issued the suspension order on Wednesday night based on the inquiry conducted by deputy commissioner of police (cyber)&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/wPxv4/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/bhagyashri-navatake" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Bhagyashri Navatake</a>.<br>The TOI on Thursday contacted the suspended woman constable for her version, but she preferred against speaking on the issue. The complainant businessman, when contacted by TOI, also avoided making any comment and said that the&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/wPxv4/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/pimpri-chinchwad" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Pimpri Chinchwad</a>&nbsp;police were already investigating the matter.<br>The police said the dealer was involved in a financial dispute with another man from Pimpri Chinchwad and the latter is on friendly terms with the constable.<br>Nearly three months back, the man asked the constable to intervene and settle the dispute for him after which the constable had called the dealer for a meeting at Wakad. This was despite the constable having no locus standi in the matter and the&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/wPxv4/https://timesofindia.indiatimes.com/topic/wakad" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Wakad</a>&nbsp;police were already examining the dispute.<br>The police said that during the meeting, the constable threatened the dealer with implicating him in a cheating case and asked him to make a transfer of cryptocurrencies in her favour if he wanted to avoid such a case and subsequent arrest.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>March 16, 2022</td><td>Pierrick Jamaux</td><td>New York, NY</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/LRGHO" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Crypto expert shot 5 times by robber seeking Richard Mille watch.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" width="869" height="515" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-179.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1016" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-179.png 869w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-179-300x178.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-179-768x455.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 869px) 100vw, 869px"></figure></div>


<p>A 33-year-old French cryptocurrency expert who was shot at point-blank range by a robber trying to steal his $450,000 Richard Mille watch says he believes he was targeted and followed for hours or days before being ambushed outside his Manhattan hotel.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Pierrick Jamaux told DailyMail.com he is shocked by how dangerous the city has become and would never have visited had he known&nbsp;how much it had changed since he lived there 10 years ago.</p>



<p>The entrepreneur, who was visiting from&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/LRGHO/https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/hong-kong/index.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Hong Kong</a>&nbsp;with&nbsp;his Australian model wife, Sarah Watts, 26, was getting out of an&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/LRGHO/https://www.dailymail.co.uk/sciencetech/uber/index.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Uber</a>&nbsp;at the&nbsp;Fifty Hotel and Suites in Midtown when he was shot five times on March 18.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Speaking from his hospital bed in New York, entrepreneur Jamaux told DailyMail.com: ‘Given the fact he was waiting there when we arrived and also the violence of the&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/LRGHO/https://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/crime/index.html" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">crime</a>, I believe he followed me.&nbsp;</p>



<p>‘I believe they found me somewhere, then they tracked me for a few hours or days to figure out what I do, where I go. I think it was organized.’</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="Pierrick Jamaux, 33, (pictured inside the ambulance) was shot five times in the legs during an attempted robbery outside his hotel in NYC" height="753" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/90b072a77a79d7af41041484f72347829b873bee.avif" width="962"></p>

<p>The attacked occurred on March 18 as the couple and another woman got out of an Uber outside the Fifty Hotel and Suites in Manhattan</p>



<p>He believes the armed robber researched the watch he was wearing, which is worth an eye-watering $450,000, before launching his attack.&nbsp;</p>



<p>He added: ‘It cannot be a coincidence because it happened between the Uber and the door of the hotel – there is two meters of distance. The guy was waiting for me there is no doubt about it.</p>



<p>‘He started shooting me even before I understood he wanted my watch and from then I was just pushing the gun down and he kept shooting my legs, it was crazy.</p>



<p>‘I know he shot five times but I think some of them went through both legs. Three of them are point-blank shooting. I have a lot of bullet holes.’</p>



<p>A 25-year-old female friend of the couple jumped on the robber’s back and began to choke him.</p>



<p>‘She is one of my really good friends, she is fiery,’ Jamaux joked, adding that she’d had a few drinks. ‘She jumped on his back and she did a triangle-like choke like in MMA.’&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>The bullets shattered his femur bone and severed his femoral artery, and he quickly passed out in the street as he began to bleed out.&nbsp;</p>



<p>The suspect was unable to wrangle the pricey watch from Jamaux’s wrist because its bracelet security mechanism. It is not clear whether the watch came with the feature or it was added.</p>



<p>The attempted robber got away with a female accomplice in a black four door sedan BMW, the NYPD says.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Miraculously, Jamaux survived the shooting,&nbsp; and credits New York hospitals’ experience with tackling shootings for his recovery.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Jamaux has since undergone six surgeries but predicts he won’t be leaving hospital anytime soon.&nbsp;</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="Jamaux works in Hong Kong for Hi, an online banking planform dealing in cryptocurrency, savings and investments" height="975" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/28d3b82e8a133029da3914706a0c19f462d7bfdf.avif" width="962"></p>

<p>‘You don’t need to be a genius to realize New York is very very dangerous right now. I don’t think it’s safe for anyone. There are too many people who have nothing to lose,’ Jamaux told DailyMail.com</p>



<p>‘They hit my femoral artery – it’s something where you usually die in 5 minutes – it was a major surgery to save my life,’ he said. ‘If you&nbsp;are going to get shot, the US is the best place to survive a gunshot wound.</p>



<p>‘I feel like the doctors really know what they are doing. I think they unfortunately have a lot of practice.</p>



<p>‘I was surprised when I talked to one of the doctors here. I said “does it happen often?” and he was like “yes” without hesitation.’</p>



<p>Jamaux lived in New York for a year about a decade ago and said the city felt safe at the time. Often on his business trips, he hires a bodyguard, but didn’t know he would need one in the Big Apple.</p>



<p>‘Because I thought New York was safe, I did not think I needed any security in New York,’ he explained. ‘A few days before the shooting we walked for one block around midnight and I did not feel safe at all.</p>



<p>‘If I knew New York had changed like that, I would never have come here. I probably would have diverted my business trip and stayed in Europe.&nbsp;</p>



<p>‘You don’t need to be a genius to realize New York is very very dangerous right now.&nbsp;I don’t think it’s safe for anyone. There are too many people who have nothing to lose.’&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>Jamaux works in Hong Kong for Hi, an online banking planform dealing in cryptocurrency, savings and investments.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>

<p>The robber got away with a female accomplice in a black four door sedan BMW, the NYPD says. The Department released this video of the getaway vehicle</p>



<p></p>



<p>The entrepreneur has also worked in Paris, where he hails from, New York City and London before he settled in Hong Kong to work with the cryptocurrency company in 2019.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>Jamaux was sporting a Richard Mille watch when the attack took place. The watches cost on average, $200,000, with some designs fetching for as much as $1.3 million.&nbsp;</p>



<p>Jamaux bought his&nbsp;for $150,000 in 2020 as an investment, and now it is now worth a cool $450,000.</p>



<p>He was staying at the Fifty Hotel and Suites on&nbsp;155 E 50th St where rooms range in price from around $350 to $1,000 per night.</p>



<p>The attempted robbery comes amid a dangerous crime wave in the once-safe city. In February there was a 60 percent spike in incidents when compared to the same period last year.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p>The city’s latest crime figures show there were 9,138 incidents last month, as opposed to 5,759 in February 2021 – with double-digit surges in nearly every major category.</p>



<p>There were 32 murders in February – three more than the same month last year.</p>



<p>Multiple other categories saw spikes, including car theft, which soared by nearly 105 percent; grand larceny, which jumped nearly 80 percent over the previous year; robberies, which surged 56 percent; a 44 percent bump in burglaries and a 22 percent spike in assaults. Rapes also saw a terrifying 35 percent rise.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="During the month of February, the NYPD reported a 58.7 percent increase in total crime" height="848" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/e3c9ca0fcca26554de8f428528f6cbc9163944c2.avif" width="962"></p>

<p>View gallery</p>



<ul>
<li></li>
</ul>



<p>During the month of February, the NYPD reported a 58.7 percent increase in total crime</p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" alt="Overall crime in the city is up more than 45 percent since the same period last year" height="1416" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/d9e026b11b40a2a823cd2b214b405d8524d41d45.avif" width="962"></p>



<p>+14</p>



<p>View gallery</p>



<ul>
<li></li>
</ul>



<p>Overall crime in the city is up more than 45 percent since the same period last year</p>



<p>Mayor Eric Adams on Sunday&nbsp;said the spike in crime across New York City has made the Big Apple a ‘laughingstock’ in need of a ‘wartime general’ to tackle the ongoing problem.</p>



<p>Adams, speaking at the annual NYPD Holy Name Society communion Mass and breakfast, condemned the lawlessness throughout the city.&nbsp;</p>



<p>He blamed petty crime and homelessness as contributing factors to the widespread ‘dysfunction.’</p>



<p>‘Anything goes in the City of New York,’ Adams said. ‘The most important city on the globe has become the laughingstock of the globe. And the dysfunctionality of our city has cascaded throughout the entire country.’&nbsp;</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>April, 2022</td><td>Unidentified trader</td><td>Dubai, UAE</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/MkVof" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">9 robbers invaded the office of a bitcoin trader and took over $1,000,000 in cash.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-180.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1019" width="868" height="974" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-180.png 657w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-180-267x300.png 267w" sizes="(max-width: 868px) 100vw, 868px"></figure></div>


<p>A gang comprising nine people stole Dh 4,120,000 from the owner of a Bitcoin trading company in the Al Nakhil area in Dubai. They assaulted him while he was at work.</p>



<p>The details of the case date back to last April, when the victim filed a report stating that he had been assaulted and robbed by force at his company’s headquarters.</p>



<p>According to the victim’s statement, he was surprised by nine robbers knocking on the door of his company and entering. They attacked him and stole the cash.</p>



<p>The police identified them and arrested them. The Dubai Criminal Court convicted them and sentenced to three years in prison, and deportation from the state after serving their sentences.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<p></p>



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>April 21, 2022</td><td>Unidentified couple</td><td>Norrköping, Sweden</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/waBom" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Couple tied up and beaten, forced to transfer cryptocurrency.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-181.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1020" width="839" height="1414" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-181.png 470w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-181-178x300.png 178w" sizes="(max-width: 839px) 100vw, 839px"></figure></div>


<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>May, 2022</td><td>4 victims</td><td>London, UK</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/rlae2" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Multiple incidents of crypto muggings around London.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-182.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1023" width="878" height="943" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-182.png 751w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-182-279x300.png 279w" sizes="(max-width: 878px) 100vw, 878px"></figure></div>


<p>Thieves are targeting digital currency investors on the street in a wave of “crypto muggings”, police have warned, with victims reporting that thousands of pounds have been stolen after their mobile phones were seized.</p>



<p>Anonymised crime reports provided to the Guardian by City of&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/rlae2/https://www.theguardian.com/uk/london" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">London</a>&nbsp;police, as part of a freedom of information request, reveal criminals are combining physical muscle with digital knowhow to part people from their cryptocurrency.</p>



<p>One victim reported they had been trying to order an Uber near London’s Liverpool Street station when muggers forced them to hand over their phone. While the gang eventually gave the phone back, the victim later realised that £5,000-worth of ethereum digital currency was missing from their account with the crypto investing platform Coinbase.</p>



<p>In another case, a man was approached by a group of people offering to sell him cocaine and agreed to go down an alley with them to do the deal. The men offered to type a number into his phone but instead accessed his cryptocurrency account, holding him against a wall and forcing him to unlock a smartphone app with facial verification. They transferred £6,000-worth of ripple, another digital currency, out of his account.</p>



<p>A third victim said he had been vomiting under a bridge when a mugger forced him to unlock his phone using a fingerprint, then changed his security settings and stole £28,700, including cryptocurrency.</p>



<p>In another case, a victim told police that his cards and phone were pickpocketed after an evening at the pub, with £10,000 later stolen from their account with the investing platform Crypto.com. The victim was using his phone in the pub and believed thieves saw him type in his account pin, the report said.</p>



<p>“It’s a sort of crypto mugging,” said David Gerard, the author of Attack on the 50 Foot Blockchain, a book on digital currencies.</p>



<p>Cryptocurrency transfers&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/rlae2/https://www.investopedia.com/articles/forex/042215/bitcoin-transactions-vs-credit-card-transactions.asp%23:~:text=Bitcoin%20transactions%20are%20irreversible%20and,when%20taking%20payment%20via%20Bitcoin." target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">are irreversible</a>, unlike a bank transfer, making this type of crime more attractive to thieves.</p>



<p>“If I get robbed and they force me to make a bank transfer, the bank can trace where the money has gone and there are all sorts of comebacks. You can reverse the transaction.</p>



<p>“With crypto, if I transfer it to my crypto wallet I’ve got your coins and you can’t get them back.”</p>



<p>He said the risks were exacerbated by the way some people handle their investments on smartphones, without exercising the same degree of caution they would with cash. “People keep stupid amounts of money on account in crypto. They don’t think it’s money somehow.”</p>



<p>Gurvais Grigg, a 23-year veteran of the FBI, now works as public sector chief technology officer for Chainalysis, which helps government agencies and financial institutions track movements of digital currency.</p>



<p>He said the nature of cryptocurrency, where transactions are logged on the blockchain, meant police should, in theory, be able to track stolen crypto.</p>



<p>“To [transfer stolen assets], they have to provide a wallet address and, most likely, they’ll use that wallet address again in the future. You also need to bring it to an exchange if you want to turn it into fiat currency.”</p>



<p>He said this created a digital paper trail that investigators can, and regularly do, use to track down multimillion-dollar crypto hacks. However, he said they were less likely to have the resources to pursue smaller, one-off crimes.</p>



<p>“An individual theft of a small amount may not get the attention of the police or a large law enforcement agency.</p>



<p>“If they could put together a larger conspiracy of activity, where people are doing it more than once or twice, police services would likely pay attention.”</p>



<p>The crypto muggings took place in the second half of 2021, in the relatively small part of London’s financial district patrolled by City of London police.</p>



<p>The incidents are not the first in which people have been forced to hand over cryptocurrency with the threat of violence.</p>



<p>A student in Kent claimed last year that eight people stormed his university accommodation and forced him to transfer £68,000 of bitcoin at knifepoint.</p>



<p>Later that year, the American technology entrepreneur Zaryn Dentzel told police he had been attacked at home in Madrid by masked thieves. He said they tortured him with a knife and stun gun before disappearing with millions of euros in bitcoin.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>May, 2022</td><td>Unidentified man</td><td>Dubai, UAE</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/Kvu77" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Crypto expert assaulted &amp; robbed by investors for losing money.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Dubai cryptocurrency expert assaulted by investors for losing money</strong></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/c95538c2bd1751612911a498959e20662105bc72.jpg" alt="Stock Dubai courts"><figcaption class="wp-element-caption">Dubai Courts.Image Credit: Gulf News Archives</figcaption></figure></div>


<p>Dubai: Six people have been sentenced to six months in jail for assaulting a Dubai-based cryptocurrency consultant and stealing his money after they lost millions of dirhams while trading with him in the digital currency.</p>



<p>According to the Dubai Court of First Instance, the six defendants stole three expensive watches and a diamond ring – worth Dh390,000 and $200,000 (Dh735,600) – before fleeing the consultant’s home in Dubai.</p>



<p>The victim claimed the defendants came to his house, assaulted him&nbsp;and stole his money and belongings after a financial dispute related to their investment in cryptocurrency. The victim said he works in the cryptocurrency business and has wide knowledge of the sector.</p>



<p>The defendants had earlier met him and asked for advise on a crypto coin called ‘Fantom’.</p>



<p>“I told them to invest in it and they did. The coin made a big profit at that time and later I asked them to sell it and they did. Then they came with others, asking me to guide them to another coin for investment,” said the victim in official records.</p>



<h3>Investment sinks</h3>



<p>He gave them another piece of advice about a new crypto coin, whose price later fell. “The coin collapsed and reached a very low level and they lost their money.”</p>



<p>They contacted him again to discuss some way to get their money back. He told them about a new coin and suggested creating a website and announcing the coin to investors to buy.</p>



<p>“They made ads for the new coin and I invested with them. The coin price went high on the launch, but only for 15 minutes,” he added. A hacker hacked the crypto coin and it reached zero dollars in value.</p>



<h3>‘They threatened to kill me’</h3>



<p>“They later came to my house and were hysteric. They threatened me and later punched me in the face. I was bleeding from my eye. They threatened to kill me and my family.”</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">

<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Manerba, threatened with a knife and robbed of bitcoins</strong></p>



<p>Three strangers followed the victim home and with an excuse one managed to enter and then force him to transfer the cryptocurrencies.&nbsp;They investigate the carabinieri</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/69a5e996e76cc109ca1125432f8cfc5edbce5021.jpg" alt="desc img" width="778" height="579"></figure></div>


<p>They managed to&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>transfer the Bitcoins to their account</strong>&nbsp;and then they disappeared on the streets of Manerba.&nbsp;This is the robbery that took place on Saturday in the town of Garda.&nbsp;Victim was a local man who was approached by at least three people.&nbsp;According to a reconstruction of the dynamics of the facts, the robbers with a trivial excuse followed the victim home.&nbsp;Then they started a generic speech and one of them managed to enter the house.At this point, the&nbsp;</p>



<p><strong>citizen of Manerba was pointed at a knife and under threat was forced to provide the codes to transfer his Bitcoins to the account of the perpetrators.&nbsp;</strong>The robbery was reported to the police, who after an inspection set off on the trail of the members of the gang.&nbsp;While the investigations are underway, there are at least three Bitcoin robbers and with the passing of the hours the Carabinieri of the Salò Company are closing in on those responsible.&nbsp;One might think that the immateriality of cryptocurrencies protects them from armed robbery.&nbsp;It is possible that some hackers will get hold of it by violating virtual wallets, as has now happened in recent years, but</p>



<p><strong>it might seem unlikely that Bitcoins would become the object of the lust of traditional robbers.&nbsp;</strong>Yet this is what happened last weekend in Manerba.&nbsp;From quantifying the money in Bitcoin that the gang managed to take away from the man’s home.In the last year, similar robberies have occurred around Europe and in Italy, but this would be the first case in the province of Brescia.&nbsp;Apparently the robbers had been monitoring the victim for a few weeks and had learned that he owned Bitcoin.&nbsp;Cryptocurrencies are a constantly expanding market also in Italy.&nbsp;According to a recent survey published in Corriere della Sera, 18% of Italians own Bitcoin or other cryptocurrencies.&nbsp;In such a context, there is another risk, namely the recycling of money through cryptocurrencies.&nbsp;Chainalysis revealed that cryptocurrency assets worth a total of $ 8.6 billion were laundered in 2021.&nbsp;This is a 25% increase compared to 2020, but a figure still lower than the peak reached in 2019, where 10,</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>August 7, 2022</td><td>Arjun Bhargav</td><td>Vrindavan Yojana, India</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/UlCSo" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">3 men trick, abduct, torture realtor for 8 BTC.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Uttar Pradesh: Three take Rs 1.3 crore ransom in bitcoins from realtor, held</strong></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-large"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" width="1024" height="611" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-185-1024x611.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1037" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-185-1024x611.png 1024w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-185-300x179.png 300w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-185-768x458.png 768w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-185.png 1159w" sizes="(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px"></figure></div>


<p>Representative Image</p>



<p>LUCKNOW: In a first-of-its-kind crime reported in the state capital, three captors of a real-estate businessman used cryptocurrency to their advantage and took a ransom of Rs 1.3 crore in bitcoins before releasing him.<br>The stunning fact emerged a week after the police arrested the three, Sandeep Pratap Singh and Vijay Pratap Singh aka Visnhu, both from neighbouring Barabanki district, and Rajveer Singh of Hardoi district. Police said that the arrested accused were in the know that the victim traded in cryptocurrency.<br>Police recovered Rs 30,000 in cash, a country-made pistol, three live cartridges, five mobile phones and a car from them. According to police, the trio abducted Arjun Bhargav, of Indraprasth Grand near Kalindi Park in Vrindavan Yojana, on the pretext of showing him a plot in Barabanki on August 7. They held him hostage at a house where they thrashed him, trained a pistol on him and got Rs 1.3 crore in bitcoins transferred to their account.<br>DCP (East Zone) Prachi Singh said the abductors, who pretended to be real estate dealers, met Bhargav and took him to Barabanki.<br>“On the way, they tied his hands and legs and took him to a house in Barabanki where they tortured him for three hours,” said Singh. The officer said the victim’s wife, Nidhi Bhargava, said in the FIR that abductors trained pistols on Bhargav forcing him to disclose the password and then got all the bitcoins transferred to their account.<br>“They also forced my husband to transfer the money into their bank account and opened fire when he resisted it. Luckily, he was not hurt. They then transported him to Lucknow and dumped him on the roadside,” she said.<br>DCP Singh said that police were tipped off by an informer about the miscreants who had abducted the businessman a week ago in a car bearing the plate of high court. “We laid a trap. On Tuesday, they visited the Kalindi Park locality probably to collect more money from the businessman. Two of them started to flee but fell at a muddy place. We nabbed them and their aide later,” she said.</p>



<p></p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>September 6, 2022</td><td>19 y/o hacker</td><td>Lincolnshire, U.K.</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/K58cR" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">3 men, 1 posing as a cop, arrested while attempting home invasion.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>



<p class="has-text-align-center has-large-font-size"><strong>Botched Crypto Mugging Lands Three U.K. Men in Jail</strong></p>



<p>Three men in the United Kingdom were arrested this month for attempting to assault a local man and steal his virtual currencies. The incident is the latest example of how certain cybercriminal communities are increasingly turning to physical violence to settle scores and disputes.</p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter is-resized"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/1012777f186c3e8efc4bdc933dc89e1ef9abef3b.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" width="870" height="481"></figure></div>


<p>Shortly after 11 p.m. on September 6, a resident in the Spalding Common area in the district of Lincolnshire, U.K. phoned police to say three men were acting suspiciously, and had jumped a nearby fence.</p>



<p>“The three men made off in a VW Golf and were shortly stopped nearby,” reads&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://www.lincs.police.uk/news/lincolnshire/news/2022/sep-2022/three-charged-after-incident-in-spalding/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">a statement</a>&nbsp;by the&nbsp;<strong>Lincolnshire Police</strong>. “The car was searched by officers who found an imitation firearm, taser, a baseball bat and police uniform in the boot.”</p>



<p><strong>Thomas Green</strong>, 23,&nbsp;<strong>Rayhan Miah</strong>, 23, and&nbsp;<strong>Leonardo Sapiano</strong>, 24 were all charged with possession of the weapons, and “<em>with intent to cause loss to another to make an unwarranted demand of Crypto Currency from a person</em>.”</p>



<p>KrebsOnSecurity has learned that the defendants were in Spalding Common to pay a surprise visit to a 19-year-old hacker known by the handles “Discoli,” “Disco Dog,” and “Chinese.” In December 2020, Discoli took credit for&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://krebsonsecurity.com/2020/12/account-hijacking-site-ogusers-hacked-again/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">hacking and leaking the user database</a>&nbsp;for OGUsers, a forum overrun with people looking to buy, sell and trade access to compromised social media accounts.</p>



<p>Reached via Telegram, Discoli confirmed that police believe the trio was trying to force their way into his home in Spalding Common, and that one of them was wearing a police uniform when they approached his residence.</p>



<p>“They were obvious about being fake police, so much so that one of our neighbours called,” Discoli said in an instant message chat. “That call led to the arrests. Their intent was for robbery/blackmail of crypto, I just happened to not be home at the time.”</p>



<p>The Lincolnshire Police declined to comment for this story, citing an ongoing investigation.</p>



<p>Discoli said he didn’t know any of the men charged, but believes they were hired by one of his enemies. And he said his would-be assailants didn’t just target him specifically.</p>



<p>“They had a list of people they wanted to hit consecutively as far as I know,” he said.</p>



<p>The foiled robbery is the latest drama tied to members of certain criminal hacking communities who are targeting one another with physical violence, by making a standing offer to pay thousands of dollars to anyone in the target’s region who agrees to carry out the assaults.</p>



<p>Last month, a 21-year-old New Jersey man was arrested and charged with stalking in connection with a federal investigation into groups of cybercriminals who are&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://krebsonsecurity.com/2022/09/violence-as-a-service-brickings-firebombings-shootings-for-hire/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">settling scores by hiring people to carry out physical attacks on their rivals</a>.</p>



<p>Prosecutors say&nbsp;<strong>Patrick McGovern-Allen</strong>&nbsp;recently participated in several of these schemes — including firing a handgun into a Pennsylvania home and torching a residence in another part of the state with a Molotov Cocktail.</p>



<p>McGovern-Allen and the three U.K. defendants are part of an online community that is at the forefront of a dangerous escalation in coercion and intimidation tactics increasingly used by competing cybercriminal groups to steal cryptocurrency from one another and to keep their rivals in check.</p>



<p>The Telegram chat channels where these young men transact have hundreds to thousands of members each, and some of the more interesting solicitations on these communities are job offers for in-person assignments and tasks that can be found if one searches for posts titled, “If you live near,” or “IRL job” — short for “in real life” job.</p>



<p>A number of these classified ads are in service of performing “brickings,” where someone is hired to visit a specific address and toss a brick through the target’s window. Indeed, prior to McGovern-Allen’s arrest, his alleged Telegram persona bragged that he’d carried out several brickings for hire.</p>



<p>Many of the individuals involved in paying others to commit these physical attacks are also frequent participants in Telegram chat channels focused singularly on&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://krebsonsecurity.com/?s=sim+swapping" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">SIM swapping</a>, a crime in which identity thieves hijack a target’s mobile phone number and use that to wrest control over the victim’s various online accounts and identities.</p>



<p>Unsurprisingly, the vast majority of people currently being targeted for brickings and other real-life physical assaults via Telegram tend to be other cybercriminals involved in SIM swapping crimes (or individuals on the periphery of that scene).</p>



<p>The United Kingdom is home to a number of young men accused of stealing millions of dollars worth of cryptocurrencies via SIM swapping.&nbsp;<strong>Joseph James O’Connor</strong>, a.k.a. “Plugwalk Joe”,&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://krebsonsecurity.com/2021/07/plugwalkjoe-does-the-perp-walk/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">was arrested in Spain in July 2021</a>&nbsp;under an FBI warrant on 10 counts of offenses related to unauthorized computer access and cyber bullying. U.S. investigators say O’Connor also played a central role in&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://krebsonsecurity.com/2020/07/whos-behind-wednesdays-epic-twitter-hack/" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">the 2020 intrusion at Twitter</a>, wherein Twitter accounts for top celebrities and public figures were forced to tweet out links to cryptocurrency scams. O’Connor is currently fighting extradition to the United States.</p>



<p><strong>Robert Lewis Barr</strong>, a 25-year-old Scottish man who allegedly stole more than $8 million worth of crypto, was arrested on an FBI warrant last year and is also fighting his extradition. U.S. investigators say Barr SIM swapped a U.S. bitcoin broker in 2017, and that he&nbsp;<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://www.scottishdailyexpress.co.uk/news/scottish-news/scot-accused-7m-crypto-fraud-27297624" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">spent much of the stolen funds throwing lavish parties at rented luxury apartments in central Glasgow</a>.</p>



<p>In many ways, these violence-as-a-service incidents are a natural extension of “<a href="https://archive.ph/o/K58cR/https://krebsonsecurity.com/?s=swatting" rel="noreferrer noopener" target="_blank">swatting</a>,” wherein fake bomb threats, hostage situations and other violent scenarios are phoned in to police as part of a scheme to trick them into visiting potentially deadly force on a target’s address. According to prosecutors, both Barr and O’Connor have a history of swatting their enemies and their SIM swapping victims.</p>



<hr class="wp-block-separator has-alpha-channel-opacity">



<figure class="wp-block-table"><table class="has-background" style="background-color:#f78da812"><tbody><tr><td>September 12, 2022</td><td>19 y/o man</td><td>Winnipeg, Canada</td><td><a href="https://archive.ph/psytU" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Man held at gunpoint, assaulted and tied up during Bitcoin trade.</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure>


<div class="wp-block-image">

<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter size-full"><img decoding="async" loading="lazy" width="783" height="811" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/image-188.png" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022" class="wp-image-1044" srcset="https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-188.png 783w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-188-290x300.png 290w, https://cryptodeeptech.ru/wp-content/uploads/2022/11/image-188-768x795.png 768w" sizes="(max-width: 783px) 100vw, 783px"></figure></div>


<h3>Two Russian husbands and wives filed a complaint against a group of six foreign men for extortion, forcing 1.8 million crypto transfers.</h3>



<p>At 9:00 a.m. on 27 Sept. 65, Pol. Col. Pongkajorn Sukksang, Superintendent of Koh Samui Police Station&nbsp;Surat Thani Province revealed that on 25 Sept. Lt. Col. Udomsak Thapha, Inspector General&nbsp;Received a complaint from Mr. Evgeny Abdullin (MR.EVGENll ABDULLIN), 31 years old, Russian national.&nbsp;And Eena Terna Abdullin (MRS.EKATERNA ABDULLIN), couples, said that on September 15, while they were using coffee at a coffee shop in the area of ​​Taling Ngam Subdistrict, Koh Samui District, Was attacked by a group of six foreign men who threatened to extort their assets in digital currency or cryptocurrencies in the amount of 50,000 US dollars, equal to 1.878 million Thai baht.By the incident that day, Mr Evgeny, the victim, said that while he was drinking coffee in the shop there was a foreign man.&nbsp;With Russian, German, and Kazakh nationality, 6 people surrounded the victims.&nbsp;And one of them was later known as Mr. Salman Almaty (MR.SALMAN ALMATY) of German nationality.&nbsp;have come to talk, claiming to have met the victims in Russia&nbsp;and threatening the victims to transfer $3 million in digital currency or cryptocurrencies.&nbsp;accounted for 112 million Thai baht, but the victim had only 58,000 US dollars of cryptocurrencies, equivalent to 2.180 million baht in Thai currency, and was afraid of physical harm, so they transferred the cryptocurrencies. Renzi amounted to US$50,000, equivalent to Thai baht 1.878 million. Salman Almaty then left his phone number and said he would come back to plow the money again.&nbsp;Before the 6 able-bodied men walked out of the shop, 5 people boarded a black van and one was riding a red Honda Click 125 brand motorcycle.</p>



<p><strong>(watch clip)</strong></p>



<p class="has-text-align-center"><video poster="https://archive.ph/VmHZx/04c6162ae30bcfd145311eda284dcd623ca3a7cf.jpg" src="data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7">t</video></p>


<div class="wp-block-image">
<figure class="aligncenter"><img decoding="async" src="./All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022 - CRYPTO DEEP TECH_files/4d5ba7e1299791589574ac7fbe3b08ddb6f5ce05.jpg" alt="All known physical attacks on Bitcoin and other cryptocurrencies from 2014 to 2022"></figure></div>


<p>Mr Evgeni, the victim, said that on September 16, 65, while driving from home to eat at a restaurant,&nbsp;On the way, he noticed that there were people following him, so he hurried home.&nbsp;And on September 18, 65, a phone call came from Telegram asking if he had been able to earn cryptocurrencies.&nbsp;If you can find it, please transfer it again.&nbsp;Or have cash to convert to cryptocurrencies?&nbsp;And to transfer through the Bybit platform, but I didn’t transfer because I didn’t have money.&nbsp;The story of this incident made himself very afraid.&nbsp;Therefore, it was decided to file a complaint with the police.Police Colonel Pongkajorn Sukksang, Superintendent of Koh Samui Police Station.&nbsp;Has ordered the police investigative team, Koh Samui Police Station, together with the Police Investigation Region 8 and the Immigration Police of Surat Thani Province.&nbsp;An investigation of CCTV footage found a van and a motorcycle identified by the victim, Afkini Abdullin.&nbsp;by checking the vehicle registration number&nbsp;It was found that the car was rented from the Pattaya area, Chonburi province, and it was expected that a group of able-bodied foreign men had left the Koh Samui area.&nbsp;Currently in the process of following up for further investigation.Pol Col Supharek Pankosol, Surat Thani Immigration Superintendent, revealed that from the investigation that&nbsp;The six foreign men, including two Kazakhstan, two Germans, one Russian and one are still under investigation.&nbsp;And from the information of traveling in and out of the Kingdom that Mr. Salman Almaty is a German national.&nbsp;Has departed Thailand via Suvarnabhumi Airport on Sept. 18 and a Kazakhstan national departed Thailand via Suvarnabhumi Airport on Sept. 20 before the victims filed a complaint to investigators.</p>
